        <p>Let f(x) = [cos(4x^2) - 1]/(x^2)</p>
        <p>Evaluate the 6th derivative at x= 0</p>
        <p><br></p>
        <p><br></p>
        <p><b>Hint:</b> Build a Maclaurin series for f(x) from the series for cos(x)</p>
        <p><br></p>
        <p>I posted this question earlier and did get a solution with the correct answer. However, dummy that I am, I can't follow the steps well enough to understand the procedure.         <p><br></p>
        <p>I know the answer is 7680 (6th derivative of f at x=0) but that does me little good. <br></p>
        <p><br></p>
        <p>Most appreciate the steps and the explanation. Also, based on the above 'hint,' does that mean we assume that we know what a Taylor series for cosine looks like? in other words, do i start with first six terms of cosine (using Taylor)</p>
        <p><br></p>
        <p>f(0) +f'(0)x + f"(0)x^2/(2!) + f'''(0)x^3/(3!)...</p>
        <p>I am confused what to do with the original function f(x) as listed above...what part do I plug in for the 'x' in the cos(x) series.</p>
        <p><br></p>
        <p>Getting myself too confused...so asking for a little clarity.</p>
